  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>The BUILTIN authentication scheme protects the passwords by hashing them with the SHA-1 algorithm. It would be nice to have way to specify a different algorithm so that users can take advantage of new, stronger algorithms provided by their JCE provider if so desired.</p> 
                  <p>This issue tracks our response to security vulnerability CVE-2009-4269, which Marcell Major identified. See <a href="http://marcellmajor.com/derbyhash.html" class="external-link" rel="nofollow">http://marcellmajor.com/derbyhash.html</a></p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

      \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"knutanders\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12838848_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=knutanders\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"knutanders\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Knut Anders Hatlen\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12838848_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'26\\/Feb\\/10 12:37\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-02-26T12:37:46+0000\'\u003e26\\/Feb\\/10 12:37\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI\'ve experimented with some code changes, see the attached patch\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nexperiment.diff, to see if it would work to implement this along the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nlines suggested above. Here\'s a description of how the patch works and\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthe behaviour we will get if we go for that approach:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eAPI and behaviour *\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eA new property called derby.authentication.builtin.algorithm is\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nintroduced. This is a dynamic property that can be set at database or\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nsystem level. The property names a digest\\/hash algorithm that must be\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nsupported by a security provider registered in the JVM.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf this property is set to a non-empty string, calls to\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nSYSCS_UTIL.SYSCS_SET_DATABASE_PROPERTY that change a password (that\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nis, set a derby.user.* property) will use the algorithm specified by\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthe property to hash the password before storing it in the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ndatabase. Otherwise, the old algorithm (based on SHA-1) is used.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSince the hashing happens when a derby.user.* property is set, a\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nchange in which algorithm to use will only take effect on passwords\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthat are changed after the algorithm was changed. This means that a\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ndatabase may contain passwords that are hashed using different\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nalgorithms. To update all the stored passwords to use the new\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nalgorithm, one has to call SYSCS_SET_DATABASE_PROPERTY again on all\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nderby.user.* properties after the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nderby.authentication.builtin.algorithm property has been set.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eErrors *\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf the derby.authentication.builtin.algorithm specifies an algorithm\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthat is not known by any of the registered security providers, an\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nSQLException with SQLState XJ001 (java exception) will be raised if a\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\npassword is attempted modified later. The SQLException is chained to a\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nNoSuchAlgorithmException.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf a stored password token for a user has been hashed with an\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nalgorithm that is not available on the current platform (could for\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nexample happen if the database was created on another platform with a\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ndifferent set of security providers), an SQLException with SQLState\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nXJ001 (java exception) will be raised when validating the credentials\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nfor that user. The SQLException is chained to a\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nNoSuchAlgorithmException.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eWe may want more specific messages in these situations. Currently, the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nmessage looks like this if you specify a non-existing algorithm, for\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nexample DOES-NOT-EXIST:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eij&gt; call syscs_util.syscs_set_database_property(\'derby.user.kah\', \'abc\');\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nERROR XJ001: Java exception: \'java.security.NoSuchAlgorithmException: DOES-NOT-EXIST MessageDigest not available\'.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eCompatibility *\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf derby.authentication.builtin.algorithm is not set or an empty\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nstring, there should be no change in behaviour.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eOtherwise, you will get the new behaviour. The new behaviour should be\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nmostly transparent to the users. However, you will no longer be able\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nto connect from the client driver with securityMechanism=8 (strong\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\npassword substitution). This is because the strong password\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nsubstitution security mechanism needs to use the same algorithm itself\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nto produce a password token that can be compared against the token\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nstored in the database.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAdding support for this on the client is not straightforward, since\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthe client would need to be told by the server which algorithm to use,\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nand this would probably require a protocol extension. It is further\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ncomplicated by the fact that the passwords can be stored with\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ndifferent hash algorithms for different users. Anyways, that\'s for\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nanother issue to address, if someone wants that functionality.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eUpgrade *\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSince earlier versions of Derby don\'t understand the new format of the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nstored password tokens, derby.authentication.builtin.algorithm is\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nignored if the data dictionary is not at version 10.6 or higher. The\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nold algorithm will be used instead in that case. This allows you to\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nchange the password of a user while running in soft upgrade mode and\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nstill be able to log in as that user if you move back to an older\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nversion of Derby.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf the database has been upgraded (with a full upgrade) so that the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ndata dictionary is at version 10.6 or later, or if the database was\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ncreated with Derby version 10.6 or later, setting the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nderby.authentication.builtin.algorithm will modify the behaviour as\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ndescribed in the sections above.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eImplementation *\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe code changes are limited to two classes (with the exception of the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ndefinition of a constant in a third one).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eAuthenticationServiceBase.java:\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe method map(), which does the mapping from plaintext password to\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nhashed password, is extended with logic to check the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nderby.authentication.builtin.algorithm property and the data\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ndictionary version in order to choose which algorithm to use.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eBasicAuthenticationServiceImpl.java:\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe method authenticateUser() is extended with logic so that it\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nunderstands which algorithm has been used to hash a stored\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\npassword. It applies the same algorithm on the user-supplied password\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nand compares it with the one stored in the database.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe existing code in these two classes already had a mechanism to\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ndistinguish between different hashing approaches. It did this by\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nprefixing the stored hash with an identifier telling which approach\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nwas used. The code in the patch piggybacked on that mechanism and\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nprefixed the tokens with a different identifier. Also, the name of the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nalgorithm (for instance SHA-256 or MD5) is appended to the token, with\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\na colon separating the hash and the name of the algorithm.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eOne somewhat confusing detail is that the old authentication scheme is\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ncalled the new authentication scheme, both in comments and names of\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nconstants. We may want to rename it to something that\'s more neutral\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nto where it is on the evolutionary path. SHA-1 authentication scheme,\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nperhaps.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFor the new authentication scheme implemented here, I tentatively\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\npicked the name \\\"configurable hash authentication scheme\\\".\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eInternal differences between the schemes *\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThere are some differences in how the hashes\\/digests are generated in\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthe two schemes, apart from the obvious that the old scheme always\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nuses SHA-1 and the new scheme can use a variety of algorithms.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eTranslating passwords into byte arrays\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe old scheme uses StringUtil.toHexByte() to convert the password to\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\na byte array. This code however assumes that all characters are within\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthe ISO-8859-1 range by only looking at the eight lower bits. It\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ndoesn\'t break when characters outside this range is used, but it does\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nnot give you any benefit from the extra bits\\/bytes you\'ve provided\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\neither. Therefore, I used String.getBytes(\\\"UTF-8\\\") instead, which is\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nsimpler and uses all bits regardless of which Unicode characters you\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nhave in your password.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eSalting the hash\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe old scheme created a hash from the password alone. This means that\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nif two users have the same password, they will have the same hashed\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\npassword. In the new scheme, the user name and the password are\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nconcatenated before applying the hash function. This means that two\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nusers with the same password will (most likely) not have the same\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nhashed password, which makes a dictionary attack more time\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nconsuming. Although it\'s not strictly necessary within the context of\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthis issue, it sounded like a cheap way to enhance the security while\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nwe\'re first at it.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFor those interested, I found this blog entry well-written and an easy\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nto understand introduction to the technique of salting password\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nhashes:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\u003ca href=\\\"http:\\/\\/pentesterconfessions.blogspot.com\\/2008\\/05\\/secure-salt-for-tastey-hashes.html\\\" class=\\\"external-link\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\u003ehttp:\\/\\/pentesterconfessions.blogspot.com\\/2008\\/05\\/secure-salt-for-tastey-hashes.html\u003c\\/a\u003e\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e(The current scheme in Derby is similar to scenario 1, described in\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthat entry, and the proposed new scheme is similar to scenario 2.)\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eComments and suggestions to improve this proposal are welcome!\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nThanks.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"knutanders\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12838848_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=knutanders\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"knutanders\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Knut Anders Hatlen\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12838848_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'26\\/Feb\\/10 12:37\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-02-26T12:37:46+0000\'\u003e26\\/Feb\\/10 12:37\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I\'ve experimented with some code changes, see the attached patch \\nexperiment.diff, to see if it would work to implement this along the \\nlines suggested above. Here\'s a description of how the patch works and \\nthe behaviour we will get if we go for that approach: \\n\\n \\n\\t API and behaviour * \\n \\n\\n\\n A new property called derby.authentication.builtin.algorithm is \\nintroduced. This is a dynamic property that can be set at database or \\nsystem level. The property names a digest\\/hash algorithm that must be \\nsupported by a security provider registered in the JVM. \\n\\n If this property is set to a non-empty string, calls to \\nSYSCS_UTIL.SYSCS_SET_DATABASE_PROPERTY that change a password (that \\nis, set a derby.user.* property) will use the algorithm specified by \\nthe property to hash the password before storing it in the \\ndatabase. Otherwise, the old algorithm (based on SHA-1) is used. \\n\\n Since the hashing happens when a derby.user.* property is set, a \\nchange in which algorithm to use will only take effect on passwords \\nthat are changed after the algorithm was changed. This means that a \\ndatabase may contain passwords that are hashed using different \\nalgorithms. To update all the stored passwords to use the new \\nalgorithm, one has to call SYSCS_SET_DATABASE_PROPERTY again on all \\nderby.user.* properties after the \\nderby.authentication.builtin.algorithm property has been set. \\n\\n \\n\\t Errors * \\n \\n\\n\\n If the derby.authentication.builtin.algorithm specifies an algorithm \\nthat is not known by any of the registered security providers, an \\nSQLException with SQLState XJ001 (java exception) will be raised if a \\npassword is attempted modified later. The SQLException is chained to a \\nNoSuchAlgorithmException. \\n\\n If a stored password token for a user has been hashed with an \\nalgorithm that is not available on the current platform (could for \\nexample happen if the database was created on another platform with a \\ndifferent set of security providers), an SQLException with SQLState \\nXJ001 (java exception) will be raised when validating the credentials \\nfor that user. The SQLException is chained to a \\nNoSuchAlgorithmException. \\n\\n We may want more specific messages in these situations. Currently, the \\nmessage looks like this if you specify a non-existing algorithm, for \\nexample DOES-NOT-EXIST: \\n\\n ij&gt; call syscs_util.syscs_set_database_property(\'derby.user.kah\', \'abc\'); \\nERROR XJ001: Java exception: \'java.security.NoSuchAlgorithmException: DOES-NOT-EXIST MessageDigest not available\'. \\n\\n \\n\\t Compatibility * \\n \\n\\n\\n If derby.authentication.builtin.algorithm is not set or an empty \\nstring, there should be no change in behaviour. \\n\\n Otherwise, you will get the new behaviour. The new behaviour should be \\nmostly transparent to the users. However, you will no longer be able \\nto connect from the client driver with securityMechanism=8 (strong \\npassword substitution). This is because the strong password \\nsubstitution security mechanism needs to use the same algorithm itself \\nto produce a password token that can be compared against the token \\nstored in the database. \\n\\n Adding support for this on the client is not straightforward, since \\nthe client would need to be told by the server which algorithm to use, \\nand this would probably require a protocol extension. It is further \\ncomplicated by the fact that the passwords can be stored with \\ndifferent hash algorithms for different users. Anyways, that\'s for \\nanother issue to address, if someone wants that functionality. \\n\\n \\n\\t Upgrade * \\n \\n\\n\\n Since earlier versions of Derby don\'t understand the new format of the \\nstored password tokens, derby.authentication.builtin.algorithm is \\nignored if the data dictionary is not at version 10.6 or higher. The \\nold algorithm will be used instead in that case. This allows you to \\nchange the password of a user while running in soft upgrade mode and \\nstill be able to log in as that user if you move back to an older \\nversion of Derby. \\n\\n If the database has been upgraded (with a full upgrade) so that the \\ndata dictionary is at version 10.6 or later, or if the database was \\ncreated with Derby version 10.6 or later, setting the \\nderby.authentication.builtin.algorithm will modify the behaviour as \\ndescribed in the sections above. \\n\\n \\n\\t Implementation * \\n \\n\\n\\n The code changes are limited to two classes (with the exception of the \\ndefinition of a constant in a third one). \\n\\n \\n\\t AuthenticationServiceBase.java: \\n \\n\\n\\n The method map(), which does the mapping from plaintext password to \\nhashed password, is extended with logic to check the \\nderby.authentication.builtin.algorithm property and the data \\ndictionary version in order to choose which algorithm to use. \\n\\n \\n\\t BasicAuthenticationServiceImpl.java: \\n \\n\\n\\n The method authenticateUser() is extended with logic so that it \\nunderstands which algorithm has been used to hash a stored \\npassword. It applies the same algorithm on the user-supplied password \\nand compares it with the one stored in the database. \\n\\n The existing code in these two classes already had a mechanism to \\ndistinguish between different hashing approaches. It did this by \\nprefixing the stored hash with an identifier telling which approach \\nwas used. The code in the patch piggybacked on that mechanism and \\nprefixed the tokens with a different identifier. Also, the name of the \\nalgorithm (for instance SHA-256 or MD5) is appended to the token, with \\na colon separating the hash and the name of the algorithm. \\n\\n One somewhat confusing detail is that the old authentication scheme is \\ncalled the new authentication scheme, both in comments and names of \\nconstants. We may want to rename it to something that\'s more neutral \\nto where it is on the evolutionary path. SHA-1 authentication scheme, \\nperhaps. \\n\\n For the new authentication scheme implemented here, I tentatively \\npicked the name \\\"configurable hash authentication scheme\\\". \\n\\n \\n\\t Internal differences between the schemes * \\n \\n\\n\\n There are some differences in how the hashes\\/digests are generated in \\nthe two schemes, apart from the obvious that the old scheme always \\nuses SHA-1 and the new scheme can use a variety of algorithms. \\n\\n \\n\\t Translating passwords into byte arrays \\n \\n\\n\\n The old scheme uses StringUtil.toHexByte() to convert the password to \\na byte array. This code however assumes that all characters are within \\nthe ISO-8859-1 range by only looking at the eight lower bits. It \\ndoesn\'t break when characters outside this range is used, but it does \\nnot give you any benefit from the extra bits\\/bytes you\'ve provided \\neither. Therefore, I used String.getBytes(\\\"UTF-8\\\") instead, which is \\nsimpler and uses all bits regardless of which Unicode characters you \\nhave in your password. \\n\\n \\n\\t Salting the hash \\n \\n\\n\\n The old scheme created a hash from the password alone. This means that \\nif two users have the same password, they will have the same hashed \\npassword. In the new scheme, the user name and the password are \\nconcatenated before applying the hash function. This means that two \\nusers with the same password will (most likely) not have the same \\nhashed password, which makes a dictionary attack more time \\nconsuming. Although it\'s not strictly necessary within the context of \\nthis issue, it sounded like a cheap way to enhance the security while \\nwe\'re first at it. \\n\\n For those interested, I found this blog entry well-written and an easy \\nto understand introduction to the technique of salting password \\nhashes: \\n http:\\/\\/pentesterconfessions.blogspot.com\\/2008\\/05\\/secure-salt-for-tastey-hashes.html  \\n\\n (The current scheme in Derby is similar to scenario 1, described in \\nthat entry, and the proposed new scheme is similar to scenario 2.) \\n\\n\\n\\n Comments and suggestions to improve this proposal are welcome! \\nThanks.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"knutanders\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Knut Anders Hatlen\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12848786_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'23\\/Mar\\/10 16:25\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-03-23T16:25:05+0000\'\u003e23\\/Mar\\/10 16:25\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eAttached is a new patch (2a) that enables the configurable hash scheme by default in new databases. The patch makes SHA-256 the default algorithm. SHA-256 is believed to be more secure than the currently used SHA-1 algorithm, and it\'s also one of the algorithms NIST recommended U.S. Government agencies to use instead of SHA-1 (see \u003ca href=\\\"http:\\/\\/csrc.nist.gov\\/groups\\/ST\\/toolkit\\/secure_hashing.html#Approved%20Algorithms\\\" class=\\\"external-link\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\u003ehttp:\\/\\/csrc.nist.gov\\/groups\\/ST\\/toolkit\\/secure_hashing.html#Approved%20Algorithms\u003c\\/a\u003e). The default algorithm can easily be changed, though, if someone thinks we should have another default. Also, it\'s possible to change the default in a future release just by changing the value of a constant, and that should not have any compatibility implications that I\'m aware of, so we won\'t be stuck forever with the algorithm we pick here.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eMaking the configurable hash authentication scheme the default authentication scheme has one known compatibility implication: Strong password substitution when exchanging credentials between the network client and the server will not work in new databases unless you manually disable the configurable hash authentication scheme first (by setting the derby.authentication.builtin.algorithm property to null). Because of this, I\'m attaching a release note as well.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eHere\'s a description of the changes made by the patch:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eiapi\\/reference\\/Property.java: added a constant for the default value (SHA-256) of the property that enables the new scheme\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eimpl\\/sql\\/catalog\\/DataDictionaryImpl.java: set the database property when the database is created (note: only on database creation, so upgraded databases will continue working the same way as before)\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003etests\\/jdbcapi\\/AuthenticationTest.java: added test case to verify that the property was initialized to SHA-256\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003etests\\/upgradeTests\\/Changes10_6.java: added test case to verify that the authentication scheme does not change on upgrade\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003etests\\/derbynet\\/NSSecurityMechanismTest.java: disable the new scheme for the test case that tests strong password substitution together with BUILTIN authentication\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAll the regression tests ran cleanly with the patch. Comments on the patch and the release note would be appreciated. Thanks.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"knutanders\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12848786_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=knutanders\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"knutanders\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Knut Anders Hatlen\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12848786_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'23\\/Mar\\/10 16:25\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-03-23T16:25:05+0000\'\u003e23\\/Mar\\/10 16:25\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Attached is a new patch (2a) that enables the configurable hash scheme by default in new databases. The patch makes SHA-256 the default algorithm. SHA-256 is believed to be more secure than the currently used SHA-1 algorithm, and it\'s also one of the algorithms NIST recommended U.S. Government agencies to use instead of SHA-1 (see  http:\\/\\/csrc.nist.gov\\/groups\\/ST\\/toolkit\\/secure_hashing.html#Approved%20Algorithms ). The default algorithm can easily be changed, though, if someone thinks we should have another default. Also, it\'s possible to change the default in a future release just by changing the value of a constant, and that should not have any compatibility implications that I\'m aware of, so we won\'t be stuck forever with the algorithm we pick here. \\n\\n Making the configurable hash authentication scheme the default authentication scheme has one known compatibility implication: Strong password substitution when exchanging credentials between the network client and the server will not work in new databases unless you manually disable the configurable hash authentication scheme first (by setting the derby.authentication.builtin.algorithm property to null). Because of this, I\'m attaching a release note as well. \\n\\n Here\'s a description of the changes made by the patch: \\n\\n \\n\\t iapi\\/reference\\/Property.java: added a constant for the default value (SHA-256) of the property that enables the new scheme \\n \\n\\n\\n \\n\\t impl\\/sql\\/catalog\\/DataDictionaryImpl.java: set the database property when the database is created (note: only on database creation, so upgraded databases will continue working the same way as before) \\n \\n\\n\\n \\n\\t tests\\/jdbcapi\\/AuthenticationTest.java: added test case to verify that the property was initialized to SHA-256 \\n \\n\\n\\n \\n\\t tests\\/upgradeTests\\/Changes10_6.java: added test case to verify that the authentication scheme does not change on upgrade \\n \\n\\n\\n \\n\\t tests\\/derbynet\\/NSSecurityMechanismTest.java: disable the new scheme for the test case that tests strong password substitution together with BUILTIN authentication \\n \\n\\n\\n All the regression tests ran cleanly with the patch. Comments on the patch and the release note would be appreciated.
